On a writer's forum I frequent, I often see the writers using AI generated images for the covers of their stories when they cant pay an artist to make one for them. To their credit they always state when it's AI generated, but they don't know the sources of the art they're getting so they can't credit the original artists which I think is the main failing of this technology. On the other hand they sometimes have to iterate so much that it's 18 layers away from what they started with to get the desired image, unlike this version that can apparently ape almost any artists style with enough input. While it's a slippery slope, the screwed up hands and often melted faces are _still_ super evident in almost every AI image, so I feel like there's still a ways to go before this is dangerously close to stealing any artists jobs permanately. Besides you still need original art for AI to generate things from, it's not going to create those waves from scratch.

Computer generated images are not art.  "Art is a selective re-creation of reality according to an artist‚Äôs metaphysical value-judgments.   Man‚Äôs profound need of art lies in the fact that his cognitive faculty is conceptual, i.e., that he acquires knowledge by means of abstractions, and needs the power to bring his widest metaphysical abstractions into his immediate, perceptual awareness. Art fulfills this need: by means of a selective re-creation, it concretizes man‚Äôs fundamental view of himself and of existence. It tells man, in effect, which aspects of his experience are to be regarded as essential, significant, important. In this sense, art teaches man how to use his consciousness. It conditions or stylizes man‚Äôs consciousness by conveying to him a certain way of looking at existence." - Ayn Rand  Only humans hold values, computers do not. Only humans can create art.  Art is objective. Shame this isn't taught in school.

When it comes to the moral question, It gets very confusing. You can get the model to reproduce styles it's never seen before. That means the style must have existed within the model before the person came up with it. So, how can anybody claim copyright over something already within the model.   The same principle can be applied to anything that was used to train the model. If you can remove any one person's work from the training data and still have it reproduce their style, then can they really own it? If anything recent developments show that just like in maths nothing is created it's just discovered.   I think copyright is essentially dead, but it's not the end of the world. Math has never had copyright yet we still have mathematicians, and they are normally paid better than artists ;-)

Clearly we need to hook up a neural net to Akinator and cross-pollinate the user feedback. Users feed Akinator new characters with names and images, other users confirm that those characters are accurate by playing the question game, all as it is today - Then the neural net accesses that name and the provided image and can use that to learn more about what that character looks like (and perhaps learn new traits based on the answers the players gave to determine which character it was in the first place). Then you can even feed that back and make Akinator provide its guesses with AI-generated images, and ask the players to rate how accurate those images are to the character they were looking for to confirm good results and weed out bad ones.

heres the thing about copying and imagination... its been prooven that our brain cannot create stuff... imagination is not something we can create out of tin air. thats why when you look at clouds and splatters you see things you already know about. like a cat, a crocodile or a buttefly...  what we call creation is the taking of two things or more and putting them together. that's what we do really... so at what point in history, not just us today, but in history... at what point can we really say its our work ? even artists that are great people today have been creating their art based on someone else, that someone who taught them how to draw.  yes they eventually designed their own art style by mixing and matching other art styles... but at which point can we say its original entirely ? just looking at our history... we can easily find source of origins going way back to our styles...   Originality is something that was lost thousands of years ago... creativity is still going strong, for the reason we have creativity, is simply us combining many things together. these AI are the proof of that, we just taught them to do it that way. because we do it that way. so to the artist who copyright their stuff... i ask... at which point do you want to stop others making money for the sake of protecting your stolen ideas ? because let's be real... all of your arts comes from somewhere that was already done before. 8 billions of people in the world... you are bound not to be the only one having thought of mixing those things and making a picture. not when you consider there isn't billions of art style that exists...   all of this is why we tell people in D&D to stop trying to create that original story, because they may be passing years developping it only to have 1 player say... its that or this... we simply tell them, go for classics, take your favorite movies and play them out. change a few things, change the world... but stop trying to be original , cause originality isn't something we can do. to me its simple... stop trying to be known by history, out of 8 billion people there is only a handful of people that will make history... and even there history will forget about them. nobody survives time.  i like imagination and the fact we can create stuff by combining other stuff...  but let's be honest.... we're not inventing anything... we're just copying mother nature !

Here‚Äôs my prediction for what it‚Äôs worth.  There will be a massive surge of this AI-generated art, but it will start to overwhelm (or at least be a significant proportion compared to) the human-generated art online. Then the AI that scans the internet for images will start to suffer from a feedback effect.  There will be three responses to this which will play out in parallel.   First, the AI generators will start to tag their art with metadata, probably identifying the software+version and the prompt used. The details don‚Äôt matter. There will be a tag in the art which will allow the image readers to exclude this art from the input, or at least to import it knowing that it was generated by AI.  Second, the studios will change what the use their concept artists for. At the moment the concept artists are given the equivalent of prompts. What you will see are artists being used to create privately held collections of art in various tagged styles. Then, when a studio wants something they can create a prompt and their instance of the software will have access to a vast private collection of labelled art to produce the required concept art, in the style the studio prefers (because that was the input) and free of any copyright claims.  Third, prompt writing will become a recognized skill in the industry. I predict that by the time this software is two years old, HR departments will be requiring five years experience of prompt writing.

The moral implications here are really sketchy to me. Like sure there‚Äôs corporations basically using this to get away with functionally stealing work from artists, but this also oddly rips away the consent of the artist.   Think about it like this, with this tech you can functionally create whatever you want with anyones style. To an extent with this AI (and those that come later) that means you can get a piece of art from an artist (or from that artist‚Äôs art) that the artist might not want to ever make. This could be as simple as having someone‚Äôs character in their style doing something the artist would want that character doing, but it could be as malicious as actively create hate speech art in the style of an artist. Sure this kind of stuff happens now with people just making art in someone‚Äôs style, but that both requires a level of craft and dedication to that design to have happen. With AI it‚Äôs easily made, and (especially when it gets better) people won‚Äôt be able to identify the difference.
Yeah‚Ä¶ this was really impressive but deeply unsettling. I‚Äôm glad you touched in it at the end. The results you were able to get are nearly indistinguishable from the art that is carefully crafted by the hands of artists, and that is a huge threat for the livelihood and careers of artists everywhere. I get that design is something that will be harder for AI to replace, but if you already had some designs, what‚Äôs stopping studios from completely replacing their concept/lookdev/storyboard artists with this infinitely alterable algorithm? This technology needs some kind of regulation at the least, and I feel like the artists that it uses to train it‚Äôs models should get royalties or something. This could very well be the death of certain art jobs and that‚Äôs very upsetting.   I saw a video yesterday that likened it to the industrial production of lace. It went from an art form that took skilled craftspeople to create to something that a machine can make incredibly fast and at very high quality standard with minima human guidance. So, then nobody bought handmade lace anymore unless they were buying it specifically because it was handmade. I don‚Äôt want that to happen to art. I don‚Äôt want human art to become something that only collectors value. Art as a career is quickly becoming endangered.
Really hope the inventors of this type of technology learn what ethics are and kill this before it truly gets out if hand.

A huge issue is even for aspects where a human artist finds a way to be unique from the AI art generators, eventually samples of that unique art (style) will still be added to the AI library.  What's interesting is that I can see a point where some visual artists actually become linguists/word smiths, and are hired for how they build queries/prompts, a role we're already seeing develop as AI art generators reach larger audiences.  Side note, Greg Rutkowski has recently been asked about his works being used in these sample sets, and there is even a growing number of artists trying to organize for change in how their art is included (or excluded) from these data sets.  It's going to be a legal mess for some time, but like almost any tech, once it's built, it's only a matter of time before it's everywhere.
I really think we have to change how we think about art. We have to see more than skill or aesthetics, see that the subjective experience of creating a piece of art has value, that the technical failures of the artist have value. AI is a cool toy, it can be fun or even inspire, but it shouldn't and can't replace the human experience of creating. This aspect, the struggle and joy of creativity, is currently undervalued, we're to focussed on the result, see it as a commodity to be cunsumed and miss why it's important, why we should still do it ourself, because not doing so would mean giving up an essential part of our culture and humanity.

Everyone is like "AI is gonna be taking our jerbs!" I have a question though. What are the two most annoying things about being a professional artist? People who scam you and people who can't make up their mind or are just bad at communicating what they want. AI art is going to fix the biggest headaches in the art biz. A good chunk of the thieves and scammers will just use AI to DIY their stuff now. And for the indecisive folks who are terriblke at communicating their ideas we can just hit them with a ton of ideas whipped up with AI. Even better the indecisive folks could do it themselves and just bring us some AI art & say, "I want THIS, but you know, GOOD." Lastly, the mainstream curiosity is going to force loads of people to be way better at their prompts because they'll get a ton of experience from spitting prompts at AI. No more rando who likes your stuff saying, "I like your style but I want this specific thing that I don't have the first clue how to describe in that style." They'll actually be able to just say, "Hey I want this exact idea, this exact pose, and I want this exact color palette in such and such style and lighting. We'll just have to adapt like we always have. AI art isn't a threat to our careers. It's just another amazing tool that will inevitably end up benefitting us more than any single group of people. Concept artists are the ones I see doing the most worrying but honestly AI art will help you guys the MOST. incredible images, mind boggling that it's AI. On the ethics of AI art tho, I think it would only be in exceptions that people should be able to call AI art "their own".  It's kind of like going to a baker, telling him what cake you want and what you want in it, and then claiming you made it yourself.
So the idea that a computer could for example use a massive dataset of artists drawing in a program and distill all the information used in the creative program then it'd be a lot less surprising it'd be capable of this. What is surprising is it can do it just from reference imagines. I think that's the deception here that we very much underestimated that super computers could literally just try every combination of that to train on what faithfully creates the image. But by the same argument then humans learn very inefficiently because of the input lag and the inability to pay attention to all the details that synthesize a great image. In otherwords since such a model is implicitly learning from us it to could make an artist learn vast amounts of information about what makes a particular artwork work. We should be thinking very carefully about what we want these models to do. Because just throwing them out on the scene like this is only possible because of the very massive amount of freely available images on the Internet. If no one is inspired to make these models work for artists and instead use them to replace artists we could just be in a world where the artwork from say 2050 is all the model has where most human artists are discouraged from ever trying to contribute.

We'll be making our own stories, with whatever actor we want! AI generated... Everything. Voice, music, video... And when it'll look SO good it goes past the uncanny valley? Then what? With such power, everyone, and I mean EVERYONE, can become everything they could ever hope to imagine! Our imagination isn't even going to be the limit anymore, because the AI will end up going even BEYOND that. And with all this on the horizon... I can't help but imagine... What will this technology give us, but also, what will it remove? When everyone's super... No-one is.

I also think artistry isn't just about drawing with a pen or pencil, or stylus. It's about having a vision for something and creating it, in some way. And some people will always be skeptical of new things, digital drawing, raw processing photos and so on.   When I was in Greenland taking pictures of icebergs this summer, I caught myself staring into the camera viewfinder 99% of the time. And at that point I thought to myself, if I could tell an AI to make the exact same picture that I take now, would I still physically go on this trip? And my conclusion was, yes I would, because of the people I met, and because when I took the camera from my eye, what I took in can't be captured on a camera sensor. It reminded me to be in the moment, and look up from the camera between shots to appreciate it.
